# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Produce answer.json** — Write ALL output to `/workspace/answer.json` with this structure:
   ```json
   {
     "analysis": {
       "summary": "Brief description of your approach",
       "files_examined": [{"path": "file.ext", "description": "..."}],
       "reasoning": "Detailed explanation or analysis"
     },
     "changes": [
       {"file": "path.ext", "description": "...", "diff": "unified diff"}
     ]
   }
   ```
   Omit `changes` if the task is analysis-only. Do NOT edit source files directly — produce diffs in `changes[]` instead.

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka SASL Authentication Mechanism Implementation

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement SASL broker-side authentication: the SASL server authenticator, the mechanism selection (PLAIN, GSSAPI, SCRAM), and the authentication context lifecycle.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{

  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the SASL broker-side authentication implementation in Apache Kafka. The answer includes:

## Summary

I've identified **28 core Java source files** implementing SASL broker-side authentication in Apache Kafka, organized into:

### **Core Authentication (1 file)**
- `SaslServerAuthenticator` - The main broker-side authenticator managing the complete authentication lifecycle with defined state transitions

### **Mechanism Implementations (13 files)**
- **PLAIN**: PlainSaslServer, PlainServerCallbackHandler, PlainLoginModule
- **SCRAM**: ScramSaslServer, ScramServerCallbackHandler, ScramMechanism, ScramLoginModule
- **GSSAPI**: KerberosClientCallbackHandler, KerberosLogin (via Java GSS framework)
- **OAuthBearer**: OAuthBearerSaslServer, OAuthBearerLoginModule, OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler

### **Configuration & Mechanism Selection (3 files)**
- `SaslChannelBuilder` - Configures and selects appropriate callback handlers
- `SaslConfigs` - SASL configuration constants
- `BrokerSecurityConfigs` - Broker-specific security configurations

### **Authentication Context & Supporting Classes (11 files)**
- `SaslAuthenticationContext` - Encapsulates authentication state passed to principal builder
- Credential management, protocol messages, exceptions, and extensions

The **mechanism selection flow** occurs in `handleHandshakeRequest()`: the client proposes a mechanism, the server validates it against the enabled mechanisms list, and creates the appropriate `SaslServer` instance. Each mechanism has its own callback handler for credential validation.

The **authentication context lifecycle** ensures the authenticated principal is built from the SaslServer through the SaslAuthenticationContext, enabling principal extrac

Client sends SaslHandshakeRequest with preferred mechanism\\n2. Server checks if mechanism is in enabledMechanisms list (from BrokerSecurityConfigs.SASL_ENABLED_MECHANISMS_CONFIG)\\n3. If not supported, server sends error response with all enabled mechanisms\\n5. createSaslServer() is called with the validated mechanism, which:\\n   - For GSSAPI: Calls createSaslKerberosServer() for Kerberos-specific setup\\n   - For others: Uses Java's Sasl.createSaslServer() with the appropriate callback handler\\n\\n### Re-authentication Support\\n\\nSaslServerAuthenticator supports connection re-authentication through reauthenticate() method with re-authentication states (REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE, REAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM) to ensure the same mechanism is used for re-authentication.\\n\"\n}\n",
